## Page 7

PROLEGOMENA

The Omnipotent and all-pervading Gayatri, Ganesa and
the Grahas have all been exceedingly merciful in enabling us
to place before the reading public this monumental treatise,
SARAVALL, with my English rendering and commentary.

Kalyana Varma, the famous author of this famous work
was a king himself ruling a place called Vyaghrapada, which
Place some of us trace in modern Madhya Pradesh and yet
some in modern Gujarat. He is also identified as Karna Deva.
He must have flourished before the 10th century as Bhattotpala
(966 A.D.) reverentially referred to our illustrious author in
his various commentaries on works like Brihat Jataka, Brihat
Samhita etc. A statement akin to our author’s date as mit
13th century is, however, incredible. Seeing Bhattotpala’s
reference and statements by various writers, our author seemed
to belong to the 6th century, that is immediately after the
Great Master, Varaha Mihira.

During the time of Kalyana Varma, there were only a
few literary gems on astrology, viz. Parasara Hora, Brihat
Jataka, Hora Sara etc. Our author feels the limitation of
Brihat Jataka (vide sloka 2, ch | infra) and has taken the
quintessence of Maharshi Parasara’s Hora Sastra, apart from
other great works like Brihat Jataka, as could be seen in
chapters like ‘Nabhasa Yogas’. The Greek pundits, Yavana-
charyas, were more often acknowledged by him, his bold
assertion of his rejecting their superfluous doctrines, being
significant (vide sloka 4 ch 1). He further remains in gratitude
to many a progenitor like Satya, Badarayana (simultaneously
the author of Brahma Sutras), Chanakya, Chudamani, Hari,
Maniththa, Brahma Saunda etc.

As the reader progresses through the work, he is sure
to feel astrologically enlightened and find an invisible preceptor
—a new source of guidance in Kalyana Varma’s words which
bequeath to us the unparallel and unsurpassed wisdom of
the sages.
## Page 8

4

The author's vast study and scientific treatment of the
subject, able exposition and inimitable style will be evident
from the provided guidelines. Apart from being an astrologer
of high latitude, the king exhibits his litcrary aptitude in the
language of the Gods, i.e. Sanscrit, through many slokas. He
was adept in traditional medicine also, vide ch. 11, dealing
with combinations to counteract lunar evils. Not only this,
he had reasonable knowledge of Yoga for Body Control, as he
refers to Basti Kriya (in ch. 11, sloka 4). (Basti Kriyais a
process of yogic cleaning of the lower intestines to strengthen
abdominal muscles and cure digestive and urinary disorders
and chronic constipation.)

‘Most later authors summarized or verbatim borrowed the
slokas of our author. Mentionable among these are : Bala-
bhadra of Hora Ratna, Vaidyanatha of Jataka Parijata and
Mantreswara of Phala Deepika apart from the author of
Jataka Saradeepa, The two works, Hora Ratna, and Jataka
Saradeepa (the latter published from Tanjore in Sanscrit),
owe a lot to Saravali.

Many important aspects of predictive astrology have
been well-explained by the author in the following pages.
Apart from ordinary preliminary information, the chapters on
Arishtas (evils) and their cancellation, combinations for
Renunciation, Nabhasa Yogas, planetary conjunction etc. may
prove ‘useful in delineation of horoscopes scientifically and
purposefully. Special mention need be made of chapters 22
through 26 which deal with effects of planets posited in various
signs. These positions stand to give modified effects if aspected
by other planets, clues to which effect have been given by the
author simultaneously. In these chapters, one finds aspects
between the Sun-Venus-Mercury mutually, in contradiction to
known principles. The author himself mentions about the
usual aspects in ch. 4, slokas 32-33. Apparently the said
aspects among Sun-Venus-Mercury are only meant to be
partial, Similar aspects continue in chapters 27-29. These dis-
cussions could be found in Hora Ratna and Jataka Saradeepa
also. As partial aspects are possible between the Sun, Mercury
and Venus mutually, one can infer that Kalyana Varma refe,.
## Page 9

by
to limited orbs only, in the relevant context. Full aspects
cannot be extended between these planets.

Extensive and useful commentary with notes and quota-
tions from a large number of texts in Sanscrit, Tamil, Telugu,
Hindi and English have been added by me in appropriate
contexts, Even the most difficult aspects have been lucidly
and minutely explained for the benefit of all concerned, accord-
ing to mymite. Though maximum efforts have been made
to keep this long-awaited treatise rid of longueurs, possibly
errors could have found their way into the text. We can only
seek the broadminded readers to view our short-comings
leniently.

The Publishers, Ranjan Publications, have follfilled
the task of this treatise seeing its print in English for the first
time in acommendable way and with their usual missionary
enthusiasm. By this act they earn the gratitude of many
anxious readers of this divine science.

We now goto the text praying Goddess Saraswati to
bestow us the required ‘digestive power’.

New Delhi Rj SANTHANAM
May 10, 1983
## Page 10

AN EPITOME OF ASTROLOGICAL NADIS

By R. Santhanam

This is a prosilient work based on many golden principles
from Nadi Treatises, brought out for the first time in English.
The reader should not mistake this for the general individual
readings by Nadi astrologers. Numerous aphorisms are given
in this text as culled out from relevant treatises, viz. Satya
Nadi, Bhrigu Nandi Nadi, Bhujanga Nadi etc.

There are many attempts, in unique and hitherto un-
published lines in this work. For example, Rahu’s sign of fall
is denoted, nay declared, as Scorpio and itis stated that if the
Moon joins Rabu in this sign, a Libran will be distressed and
dullwitted. In view of the fact that Ayanamsa is the
main key to all the principles in this text, one sign
having been made into 150 equal divisions, the aathor,
Sri Santhanam, has ably and convincingly solved the
vexed precisional problem and the reader is rightly
guided to use these priaciples with the right Ayanamsa,
It is hoped that this work will be very warmly received by the
astrological fraternity.

THE SECRETS OF ASHTAKAVARGA

By R. Santhanam

An unassumingly original treatise compiled by Acharya
Mukunda Daivagna of Gharwal in Sanscrit, during his Ashram
life. His work NASHTA JATAKAM with Mr. Santhanam’s
English translation is already familiar to the readers. Our
preseat attempt is to expand the availability of Mukunda’s
magnificent treatises to one and all. Mukunda Daivagna was
none other than Mukunda Rama, the illustrious commentator
of Prasna Gnana, under the name of Aryasapthati, Reference
to Aryasapthati with reverence could be found in late Sri
V. Subramanya Sastri’s preface to bis English translation of
Prasna Gnana.
## Page 11

7

The work in original has eleven chapters in 455 Devanagari
verses. To mention captions of chapters, some are : Graha and
Bhava. Janyashtaka Vargas, Ashtaka Varga Dasa, Ashtaka
Vargarishta etc. The original has been constructed with addi-
tional help from Deva Keralam, Viswanatha Kavi, Brahma
Yaamala; Prithu Yasas, Karana (@<q) Prakasa, Kalyana Varma,
Jaganmohana, Devasala etc.

The translator who christened the work as above,
expanded the work further so that a majority of pastmasters
are put together to express their views in one single work.
Reliable quotations and scholarly commentaries adore this
rich work. Hereis a golden opportunity for the lovers of
Hindu Astrology, particularly those who enjoy the Ashtaka-
varga method of prognastication for natal and transit charts.
This work in a way is a propylacum of astrology.

DOCTRINES OF SUKA NADI

By R. Sarthanam

‘An excellent and rare work containing principles on
predictive astrology. Exclusive aphorisms from authoritative
treatises on Hindu Astrology fully enrich this work, To
cite an instance : If the lords of the Sth and the 8th join in the
7th along with Saturn and Rahu, the female concerned does not
attain puberty at all. In another context, it is stated that if a
movable Rasi ascend containing the 8th lord therein, the native
enjoys full span of life. These are specific and exceptional
roles and the author has explained the rationale behind such
principles.

This work touches all houses including clues to time
events, principles covering marital match and such other

aspects. An indispensible work to those who breathe astrology
at all times
## Page 12

8
BHRIGU SUTRAM

Just as the celestial bodies represent the Almighty so
does a sage in many ways. Bhrigu Rishi with his divine insight,
not fruitfully possessed by an ordinary immortal, created this
work in simple Sutras. The Sanskrit principles by the sage
are not only astrologically rich but are very terse and are
capable of being committed to even ordinaty memory. The
advantage ; these rules pregnant of useful meanings can be at
one’s back and call.

Dealt with by the sage in the text are : the results of
various planets in each bhava along with many yogas. The
English translation includes detailed comments, the technique
of application and correlated views of other classicals.

This work abridges the lacuna in predictive astrology.

BRIHAT PARASARA HORA
OF SAGE PARASARA
(Sanskrit Verses with English translation)

This isa great traditional treatise on eastern astrology.

The science of astrology in the east took its incarnation

through the divine insight of Parasara, the Father of Hindu
Astrology.

The present English version is the first ever attempt in
the press of the world, To highlight briefly, the work deals
with basic aphorisms of Hindu astrology extending to difficult
and minute sides of the subject. Aspects emanating from
signs (a peculiarity to Parasari system), effects of sub planets
(a great discovery by Indian astrologers), a number of
systems relating to dasa periods, Ashtaka Varga, exclusive
rules for nativities of the fair sex, methods to locate lost birth
data, planetary rays, effects of births at eclipses, New Moon
etc. planetary locations in various houses and many such
other valuable information are full in this work.

The present version runs voluminously into 97 chapters
and hence is byfar the largest edition.

The work is translated in English by R. Santhanam by
whom no stone is left unturned in enlightening every difficult
stanza with clarifications. This isa widely acclaimed treatise
and is most sought after by the students and savants of astro-
logy.
## Page 13

9
PRASNA MARGA

This eternal classic occupies a high position of pride in
the chrest of the peacock of Hindu Astrology. Just as one
cannot take pleasure at the peacock’s chrest unless it is thrown
wide open, the riches of our astrology will not be discovered
without entering in the mines of works like Prasna Marga.
The farther one is from such literature, the darker the secrets
ofthis super science. Prasna Marga took its birth through
an extremely intelligent astrologer of Kerala during the 16th
century.

The author presents the short and the long of many
standard traditional astral literature of those days including
KRISHNEEYAM. Though the name of the text looks as if
it deals with (only) Horary astrology, it does as well deal with
natal astrology, Karma, Remedial Measures etc. in great and
possible detail. A ‘significant importance has been given to
Mantra Sastra also.

Ashta Mangala Prasna, a peculiarity which has been
successfully encashed by Kerala astrologers, can be found
exclusively in Keralite literature like the present work. Ina
way, Ashta Mangala Prasna is Hindu numerology. Exhaustive
chapters are devoted to diseases, omens, Trisphutas, Kala-
chakra Dasa, spirits, matrimony rains, silent questions (Mooka
Prasna—a system to know what the query is when untold),
dreams, Ashtaka Varga etc. All the chapters have received
scholarly treatment in the hands of the author. The
32 chapters are thus divided in 3 volumes with easily
understandable English translation and commentary by
Sri J.N. Bhasin and in Hindi by Sri Sukdev Chaturvedi.

JATAKA PARIJATA

The reader will be convinced that the work in question
is among the most essential ones if one aims at perfect mastery.

This work is one of the greatest classics in the series of
of classical astrology we inherit from our pastmasters. The
author is Venkatesa Daivagna’s son, Vaidyanatha. The former
authored Sarvartha Chintamani which is also full of instructive
and suggestive rules on predictive astrology, Vaidyanatha in
his text gives the quintessence of Garga Hora, Parasara Hora,
## Page 14

10

Brihat Jataka, Hora Sara, Sarvartha Chintamani etc. and has
covered many sections on horoscopy in a systematic and lucid
manner, in as many as 1900 slokas in Sanskrit.

Apart from covering elementary aspects for a student’s
easy grasp, the text deals with the properties of each zodiacal
sign and of the planets, their nature, combinations to curtail
or bestowing good longevity. combinations of planets to mar
a nativity, those that confer position. effects of two and more
planets, effects of Gulika, effects of births in the sixty Jovian
years (Brahaspathya Varsha), effects of births in various asteri-
sms, details of results of Ashtaka Vargas, the 12 houses, female
horoscopy, and various kinds of planetary periods. The great-
ness of this work lies in each and every chapter.

The English translator, late Pandita Vidyabhushana
Subramanya Sastri gives simple account with notes and
examples. Students and scholars alike enjoy this work and
derive benefits galore.

SATYA JATAKA

Sage Satyacharya, reveredly quoted by Varaha Mihira,
Prithu Yasas, Kalyana Varama, Balabhadra etc.—pillars of
Hindu astrology—in their works, lays down exemplary and
scientific principles through this monumental piece on predictive
astrology. These were originally communicated by Dhruva to
Jaimini, the latter to Garga, from whom Sage Vyasa acquired
these. Sage Vyasa taught this science to Satya. Bhattotpala,
the celebrated commentator of Varaha Mihira, quotes many
of these slokas in his commentary on Brihat Jataka.

Satya Jatakam contains many unique and not-much-
known principles. Significance of planets, Pancha Siddhanta
criterions, results of house lords in various houses, rules for
study of Navamsa chart, Planetary transits, effects of planetary
periods with reference to different houses, longevity calcula-
tions, combinations for kingship and various such other relative
and reliable information that goto benefit an astrologer are
summarized in this work.

The English translation is enriched by an addition of
important Sanskrit slokas (with English translation) from
Bhattotpala’s commentary on Brihat Jataka as well as Chinta-
mani commentary. The ultimate beneficiary is the reader who
is always in search of Truth.

GARGA HORA
By Sage Garga (English Edition)

Sage, Garga, an offspring of Brahma, the Creator 0
Universe, composed various astrological principles through
his divine insight. Just as the planetary indications never err,
60 also the words of the sages.

Sage Garga has deviced exclusive principles dealing with
results of planetary combinations of all possible permutations,
‘These relate to the 12 houses in groups of planets ranging from
two to seven. Other very useful clues to aspects of predicative
astrology are also discussed in this old classic. A total of
over 1400 principles are found in this work.

The English edition is prepared by R. Santhanam with
suitable notes and clarifications. This work is a must for every
student wanting to possess authoritative information.

NASHTA JATAKAM
By Achary Makanda Drivagoa
(Sanskrit-English)

Tracing unrecorded date of birth and time is no more a
problem. The author, Mukunda Daivagna has enunciated a
great number of fool-proof methods after a study of the
schools of Varaha Mihira, Kalyana Varma and others. Many
such rules have been well-developed by him and are taught
to the student in an explicit manner. The Kerala system of
Lost Horoscopy in the 3rd chapter paves 22 different ways, to
reach the route of the riddle, i.e. working out the year of
birth, planetary season, month, thithi, nakshatra, ascendant,
navamsa etc. and wonderfully enough even the planetary
positions at birth.

Many new rectification methods are added in the fourth
chapter to help one arrive at a doubtless horoscope, A
number of people achieved success in knowing their lost
horoscopes with the help of this first ever published and unique
monumental.

‘The English translation is by R. Santhanam, who has
added exhaustive appendix with much fmore relevant infor-
mation in this direction. This appendix deals, inter alia, with
effects of births in the 108 navamsas and additional classical
methods to trace a lost:horoscope,

Nadi System of Prediction (Stellar Theory)

their pratical worth, their ability to withstand the test of ex-

which will considerably satisfy the readers who want to gain,

Chapter 1 Birth of Horasasthra

1. Glory to the Sua God, whose very breathing causes
Creation in this world, with whose rising all the animals
(living beings) wake up (from the sleep of their ignorance),
whose state at the head (i.e. zenith) accentuates all activities
(throws the brightest light on one’s wisdom) and whose setting
(absence or weakness) causes all to sleep, Such Sun God has his
efficacy spread (all over).

Notes: Most of the astrological savants in recognition
of the importance of the Sun, praise him in the beginning of
their works. Kalyana Varma, the king-astrologer, throws
light on the Sun’s importance in all daily walks of life. The
Sun’s rise releases one of his night sleep and imparts’“‘creation””
* in his daily activities. Similarly, if the Sua, at birth, is on the
east, he bestows creative power on the fe. When the Sun
reaches the head at noon, human activities are at height.
Likewise, when he is in the Zenith in the horoscope of birth
(ie. om the 10th cusp), one is likely to reach enviable heights
## Page 22

18 Saravali

in life When the Sun sets, the day ends, breaking the vigour
of the day while in the horoscope, the Sun in the setting
house (7th house) or in a weak state, reduces the force of
other heavenly bodies. That is why Prithuyasas etc. state
that the strength of the Sun is very much essential in order
that other Yogas become efficacious for the native.

We can also see that most authors, e.g. Varaha Mihira,
Prithuyasas etc, praised the Sun God in the opening slokas, in
their famous astrological works.

2-4, Varaha Mihira in his Hora Sasthra i.e. Brihat Jataka
stated briefly the essence of the teachings of the learned sages,
viz ten divisions of the zodiac (za ai), Raja Yogas, longevity,
effects of planetary periods etc. This could not be done elabo-
rately by him and hence I (Kalyana Varma) am conveying in
this work such useful essence as culled out from Yavanas etc.
rejecting other unuseful portions, which may be appended to
the said Brihat Jataka,

Notes : The author, Kalyana Varma, has studied Brihat
Jataka etc. and gives in this work various principles for the
sake of the students of astrology.

1-S; The Creator, Brahma, has written on the foreheads
of all living beings their fates which are deciphered by the as-
ttologers through their pure insight. The first and last letters in
the word wetzrz (i.e. day and night) are removed and the word
“@tzr” is thus born and has come to exist. The zodiac and
the planets are therein as sussed (in these pages). Some
scholars say Hora Sastra is indicative of effects of one’s Karma
i.e. fate. Some call Lagna or half of a Rasias Hora. In
ptactice, the science relating to horoscope is called Hora
Sasthra. Hora is capable of anyalising the destiny. Barring
this Hora Sastra (i.¢. Astrology) there is no device to help
one earn money, to help as abost to cross the ocean of
unexpected situations and to serve as an advisor in journey.

Notes: The purpose of astrology is to assess one’s
livelihood, bad and good incidents in life, journey etc. before
hand and plan life suitably.

Sze Brihat Jataka, Chapter I, Sloka 3, which states that
whatever has been acquired by a person through his past deeds
—good or bad—now attain fruition. See what a1%z (Narada)
States : AMAA FUT Faadiwaiag, meaning that with-
out the kn.wledge of birth time, i.e. sans a horoscope, it is akin
to describing an incision in wood or a book. These show the
importance of Hora Sastra or the Science of Astrology.

1-2. At the time of Pralaya ("4, i.e. Destruction), the
Universe plunged into darkness and was. flooded with water,
when, all of a sudden, the Sun God, with his brilliant rays
appeared in the Universe. He created all the planets and the
12 months.

Notes: Each solar month is the result of the Sun’s
movement in a particular Rasi and 12 solar months are caused
during his sojourn in the 12 Rasis of the zodiac.

DESCRIPTION OF THE 12 RASIS

3-4. The names of the 12 Rasis are : Aries, Taurus,
Gemini, Cancer, Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio, Sagittarius, Capri-
corn, Aquarius and Piscss. The sign Aquarius resembles a man
holding a pot while Gemini is compared to a couple holding
Veena (qT) and mace (721). A pair of fish is the imagi-
## Page 26

2 Saravali

nation about Pisces. Sagittarius is compared to a man, having a
hip like that of a horse and holding an arch in his hands. Deer-
faced sign is Capricorn, Virgo resembles a virgin sitting ina
boat with a lamp in her hands. A male holding Seales in hand
represents Libra. The other signs are identical with theirnames.

5-6. THE LIMBS OF KALA PURUSHA AND THEIR USE :
The signs Aries etc. represent the limbs of Kalapurusha as
under :

Aries: head; Taurus: face; Gemini : arms; Cancer:
heart; Leo: stomach; Virgo: hip; Libra: space below navel
and private parts; Scorpio : private parts; Sagittarius ; thighs;
Capricorn : knees; Aquarius : ankles; Pisces: feet. If at birth,
one has benefic planet in a particular sign, the particular limb
will be strong. A malefic makes such a limb weak.

Notes : While for Kalapurusha, the respective limbs are
identified from Aries onwards, for an individual, apart from
considering the Rasis as above, one should count from the
natal lagna also. For example, suppose one is born in Leo.
This sign indicates his head. Hence, when assessing the head of
a Leo native, look at Leo and Aries as well,

Hridaya Roga, and Anthya are the other names given respecti-
vely to Rasis from Aries onwards.

Notes: Such other synonyms can be found in Brihat
Jataka, Hora Sara, Hora Ratna, Phala Deepika etc.

9-10. ZODIACAL HALVES, THEIR LORDS, AND
EFFECTS : The Rasi chakra with 12 Rasis is called Bhagana
(aq). Six sigas counted from Leo to Capricorn consist of
Solar Half and the Sun rules this qo wm (Half Zodiac). « Six
signs in the reverse order from Cancer to Aquarius is Lunar
Half and ruled by the Moon. Barring Cancer and Leo, planets
from Mars to Saturn get one Rasi each in each Half, as
above. If at birth more planets occupy the Solar Half, the
native is brilliant, and if more planets are in Lunar Half, he
is soft, good and lucky.

Notes : If a majority of planets are placed from Leo to
“Capricorn, the native acquires the qualities of the Sun. Should
a majority be disposed from Aquarius to Cancer (via'Pisces),
the native begets Moon’s disposition, The former makes one
splendorous and valorous while the latter makes one soft-
spoken and fortunate.

11. THE RULERS OF RASIS AND NAVAMASAS :
Mars, Venus, Mercury, Moon, Sun, Mercury, Venus, Mars,
Jupiter, Saturn, Saturn and Jupiter are the lords respectivelysof

Aries to Pisces. The Navamsas for these Rasis are calculated
from Aries, Capricorn, Libra and Cancer in their order.
## Page 28

24 Saravali

Notes : How to calculate the Navamsa positions is
explained below =

Each Rasi has nine Navamsas of 3°-20' each, The coun-
ting for Aries, Leo and Sagittarius is done from Aries itself.
It is done from Capricorn for the signs Taurus, Virgo and
Capricorn. For Gemini, Libra and Aquarius, the counting is
commenced from Libra. The Navamsas of Cancer, Scorpio and
Pisces range from Cancer.

Another method is to count from stellar quarters. Take
the first 3 stars or 12 quarters and count from Aries and con-
clude with Pisces. Proceed in the same manner for each group
of 3 stars again and again.

That is, Aswini-Bharani-Krittika form one group the
Navamsas of which range from Aries to Pisces. Then again
proceed in the same way for Rohini-Mrigasira-Aridra group
and for other groups.

12, SUB-DIVISIONS ESSENTIAL: The effects of a
horoscope should be predicted according to the divisions of
houses. Without knowing the strength of such lords, one cannot
lay even a step forward in the direction of astrology.

13. VARGOTHAMAMSA : The first Navamsa of a
Movable Rasi, the Sth one in a Fixed Rasi and the th one in a
Common Rasi (dual sign) are called Vargothamamsas. Should
the natal Lagna be in such Vargothama Navamsa, the native
becomes an important person in his circle. The rulers of
Dwadasamsas start from that Rasi itself.

25

Aswini I quarter (Aries)
Rohini I quarter : (Taurus)

Pubba I quarter (Leo)
Chitta I quarter : (Virgo)
Chitta IL quarter : (Libra)

Uttarashadha =-‘I quarter : (Capricorn)

Revati IV quarter : (Pisces)
Dwadasamsas: Each Rasi is divided into 12 Dwada-

‘samsas of 2° 30’ each. The first one falls in that Rasi itself,
the second one in the second from there, the third one in the
third from there and so on and so forth. These are tabulated
on page No. 26.

14. LORDS OF DECANATES AND HORAS : The lords
of decanates are: First decanate—lord of the same Rasi, second
decanate—lord of the Sth Rasi therefrom and third decanate—
lord of the 9th from the Rasi in question. The first Hora of an
odd Rasi belongs to the Sun while the second one is ruled by
the Moon. In the case of an even Rasi, the first Hora is ruled
by the Moon and the second Hora by the Sun.

Notes: Decanates: Each Rasi is made in three equal
parts of 10° each. The three are respectively lorded by the
Ast, 5th and 9th lords therefrom. See table on page No. 27.

Suppose a planet is in 12° of Pisces, which means it is
in the second decanate. The second decanate of Pisces falls
in Cancer and the ruler thereof is the Moon.

HORAS : Each Rasi is divided in two equal parts of 15°.
The first Hora of an odd Rasi is ruled by the Sun and the
second by Moon. In the case of even Rasis, the first and second
Horas are respectively ruled by the Moon and the Sun. See
the Table below :

Rasi. It is in the second Hora ruled by the Sua.

15. LORDS OF TRIMSAMSAS :

In odd signs, 5, 5, 8,7 and 5 degrees are Trimsamsas of

Mars, Saturn, Jupiter, Mercury and Venus respectively while
the arrangement is reverse in even signs.

Notes: The Sun and the Moon have no lordship over
Trimsamsa division. Now see the table as under :
## Page 33

Chapter 3 2»

Odd Signs Even Signs
up to 5° Mars up to 5° Venus
S* I’ to 10° Saturn ul ghz Mercury
10° 1’ to 18’ Jupiter 12° 1’to 20° Jupiter
18° 1’ to 25° Mercury 20° 1’ to 25° Saturo
25° 1’ to 30° Venus 25° 1’ to 30° Mars

Suppose a planet is at 28° of an odd sign, then it falls
Venusian Trimsamsa, If it is in 8° of an even siga, then the
Trimsamsa belongs to Mercury.

In the context of Female Horoscopy, these positions
are very useful. See chapter 46 for details.

16. LORDS OF SAPTAMSNS : The Saptamsas for the
12 Rasis from Aries onwards are respectively counted from
Aries, Scorpio, Gemini, Capricorn, Leo, Pisces, Libra, Taurus,
Sagittarius, Cancer, Aquarius and Virgo. The lords thereof
are those in whose Rasis they fall.

Notes; The idea is that the counting of Saptamsa for
odd'signs starts from that sign itself. In the case of even Rasis,
it is from the opposite house. For example, the counting of
1/7th Amsa starts from Leo itself for Leo, the second is Virgo,
third is Libra and soon and so forth. For Cancer, an even
Rasi, the counting is done from Capricorn, Each Rasi is
made in seven equal parts to be called as Saptamsa. Each
Saptamsa thus equals to 4°17' 84”.

Till now in the previous pages, we have had the following
divisions :

1. Rasi_ 2. Hora 3, Drekkana 4. Navamsa 5. Dwa-
dasamsa 6. Trimsamsa 7. Saptamamsa. There are other
niné esseatial divisions to complete the Shodasa Varga (16
Varga) scheme. Some are satisfied with 10 Vargas and yet
## Page 34

30

some with 7 Vargas, For the information of the readers, the
lacuna is completed as under :

(8). Turvamsa : Each sign is made in four equal parts of
T° 30’ cach. The first Turyamsa is lorded by the lord of the
same Rasi, the second one by the lord of the 4th sign, the
third one by the lord of the 7th sign and the 4th one by the
lord of 10th sign, For example, the lords of 4 Tuyramsas in
Aries are respectively : i

Mars (Aries), Moon (Cancer), Venus (Libra) and Saturn
(Capricorn). Similarly, for other positions in various Rasis
these may be noted. .

(9) Dasamsa : Each Rasi is divided in 10 parts of 3°
each. In odd signs, the counting is from the sign itself. For
even signs, the counting is from the ninth thereof, For example,
the Ist Dasamsa of Aries, is in Aries itself, the 2nd in Taurus,
the 3rd in Gemini and so on and so forth, Take Scorpio an
eyen Rasi. Its first Dasamsa falls in Cancer which is the 9th
Rasi from Scorpio. The second falls in Leo, the third in
Virgo, the fourth in Libra and so on and so forth. ’

(10) Shodasamsa (i.e. 1/16th of a Rasi): This, is also
called Khalaamsa. Each Rasi is made in 16 equal parts i,e,,
1g degrees. The counting commences from Aries for Chara
Rasis, from Leo for Sthira Rasis and from Sagittarius for’ Dwi-
swabhava Rasis. To give an example, in the case of movable
signs, the first Shodasamsa is Aries, the 2ndis Taurus, and so
on; the 13th is again Aries, the 14th is again Taurus the 15th is
again Gemini and the last one, 16th is again Cancer. Similar
calculations should be made for fixed and dual (common) signs
accordingly.

(11) Viowsamsa : Bach Basi is tnade in 20 equal partveach
of 1°30’. The counting for movable signs commences from
Aries, for dual signs from Sagittarius and for common sign’
from Leo: For example take a common sign, for which
counting is to'be done from Leo. The first, Vimsamsa-is. dn
theo, the second in Virgo, the 12th in Cancer, the 13th in
Keo again arid soon and so forth, with the 20th Vimsamsa
## Page 35

Chapter 3 31

ending in Pisces. Similarly, for other signs, suitable deductions
can be made.

(12) .Chaturvimsamsa: Each Rasi is made in 24 equal
parts. This is also called Siddhamsa. One such division is
made up of 1° 15’ of arc. For odd signs, the 24 divisions are
counted from Leo while for even signs the counting is from
Cancer. For example, the first Siddhamsa of Aries is Leo,
the 2nd is Virgo, the 3rd is Libra, the 13th is again Leo, the
14th is Virgo while the 24th one is Cancer. In the case of
Taurus, an even sign, the Ist one is Cancer, the 2nd one is
Leo, the 3rd one is Virgo, the 12th one is Gemini, the 13th
is again Cancer, the 14th is again Leo while the 24th is again
Gemini. The intermediary ones may be suitably understood
accordingly. ;

(13) Nakshatramsa or Sapthavimsamsa: This is 1/27th
part of a Rasi. The counting starts from the Rasi itself,
whether it is an odd one or an even one. For example, for
Aries, start from Aries and count upto Pisces, you get 12
Sapthavimsamsas. Then the 13th one is again Aries, the 14th is
Taurus, the 24th is Pisces, the 25th is again Aries, the 26th one
is Taurus and the 27th one is Gemini.

(14) Swa-Vedamsa : Bach Rasi is made in 40 equal parts,
each of 45’ of arc. The counting for odd signs commences
from Aries while Libra is the starting point for even signs.
For example, for odd Rasis, we complete 3 rounds from Aries
to Pisces to get 36 Swavedamsas. The 37th one is again Aries,
the 38th one is Taurus, the 39th one is Gemini and the 40th
one is Cancer.. Similarly for even Rasis, starting from Libra,
we complete 3 rounds upto Virgo to get 36 Swavedamsas. The
37th, 38th, 39th, and the 40th ones are respectively Libra,
Scorpio, Sagittarius and Capricorn.

(15) Akshavedamsas : Each Rasi is divided into 45 equal
parts, each of 40’ of arc. In the case of movable Rasis, the
rulership is counted from Aries; from Leo in so far as fixed
Rasis are concerned and from Sagittarius for dual signs,
## Page 36

32

each Rasi has 60 such Shashtiamsas.

one of odd Rasi will be the first one of even Rasi. The second

Saptavargas : These consist of Rasi, Hora, Decanat e,
Sapthamsa, Navamsa, Dvadasamsa and Trimsamsa.

Dasa Vargas: Khalamsa, Dasamsa and Shashtiamsa
calculations are added to the above-mentioned Sapthavarga
scheme, to get Dasavargas.

Shodasa Vargas : These are sixteen divisions, which
Ihave explained in the previous pages.

The use of the said 16 vargas is explained below :

(1) Rasi Lagna Appearance, shape, etc,

(2) Hora Financial status

(3) Decanate Brothers and happiness from them
(4) Turyamsa Bhagya or prosperity

(5) Sapthamsa Children and grand children
(6) Navamsa Wife

(7) Dasamsa Profession

(8) Dvadasamsa Father and mother

(9) Khalamsa Conveyances

(10) Vimsamsa Success

(11) Chaturvimsamsa Education

(12) Nakshatramsa Strength

(13) Trimsamsa Malefic results

(14) Swavedamsa Good and,.bad

(15} Akshavedamsa Good and bad

(16) Shashtiamsa Good and bad

17. The total of the number of Horas and that of deca-
nates is sixty (24-+36), inthe entire Zodiac. The figure is
increased by 72 if the total of Horas-+Navamsas is required,
ie. 60+72=24+108=132. Each Rasi has 1800 Kalas (30
degrees each of 60’ of arc).
## Page 38

34 Saravali

arardtat frat Ram: eagrfeartag frat: 1
agreratawaat tea: eardtftad) at: ues

18. DIFFERENT VARGAS : To know any kind of Varga
(ie. Hora, Navamsa, Drekkana etc.) adopt the following
method : convert the longitude into minutes of arc and multi-
ply by the Varga figure concerned. Divide the product by
1800. The resultant figure will reveal the required Varga.

Notes : Suppose a planet is in 15° of Aries and we want
to know the Navamsa position. 15° converted into:minutes
becomes 900 This should be multiplied by 9 which is the
figure for Navamsa, We get 8100. Divided by 1800, this
yields 4 completed Navamsas with a remainder which indicates
the Sth Navamsa. The factor of multiplication for Hora is 2,
for decanate 3, for Dasamsa 10 and so on and so forth. These
Vargas can be found from the tables already given earlier
without undergoing this ordalium.

wast quater faeacat agora aet 1

19, The malefic and benefic effects of such Vargas are

20-21. RASIS—BENEFIC AND MALEFIC IN NATURE;
GANDANTA AND ITS EFFECTS : From Aries onwards, alter-
natively the Rasis are known as malefic and benefic on the one
hand, and male and female on the other band. These are also
classified as chara (Movable), Sthira (Fixed or Immovable) and
Dyiswabhava (Ubhaya, dual or common) Rasis. The ending
portions of Cancer, Scorpio and Pisces are called Gandanta.
It is said that one born in Gandanta will not survive. He will
either lose his mother or he will end the dynasty, i.e. he is
the last of his descent and will not have any children, Jf,
## Page 39

Chapter 3 35

however, he survives, he becomes a king with many elephants
and horses.

Notes : The Rasis are classified as under :

Aries odd male
Taurus even female
Gemini odd male
Cancer even female
Leo . odd male
Virgo even female
Libra odd male
Scorpio even female
Sagittarius odd male
Capricorn even female
Aquarius odd male
Pisces even female

Gandanta : For Gandanta, I have given elaborate notes
in my translation of Horasara, vide chapter 5 which the reader
may consult,

22, DIRECTIONS OF RASIS : The four Rasis from
Aries onwards indicate East, South, West and North, while
the remaining Rasis repeat in the same way. A journey under-
taken by a person towards the direction indicated by the Lagna
or the Moon (at the commencement of journey) yields fruitful
results.

Notes: According to the above rule, for example, if
“Aries is the Lagna at the commencement ofa journey, or if
the Moon be in Aries, there is success in the eastern direction,

Now, the directions indicated in this Sloka are :

Aries, Leo and Sagittarius East
Taurus, Virgo and Capricorn South
Gemini, Libra and Aquarius West

Cancer, Scorpio and Pisces North

23. DIGBALA AND KALABALA : Human signs, quad-
ruped signs, Scorpio and watery signs are respectively strong in
the directions commencing from the east. Further during night
time quardruped signs, day time human or biped signs and the
second half of Capricorn, Scorpio, Cancer and Pisces are strong
at the time of day break and or night fall .

Notes : Digbala of signs: Each Rasi assumes strength
when it happens to be a certain Bhava. East represents Lagna,
South represents the 10th house, West represents the 7th house
(ie. the opposite of Lagna) while the 4th house (i.e. opposite
of the 10th, the South) is the North.

The northern point is also called Nadir; the Western point
is known as descendant and the southern point is the zenith of
the horoscope. The ascendant and the planets (from the Sun
to Saturn) in their usual motion move from East to West via
the North. That is their motion is anticlockwise. Rahu, Ketu
and others (i.e. Mars to Saturn) when retrograde move from
West to East via North i,c. clockwise,
## Page 41

Chapter 3 37
Human signs are: Gemini, Virgo, Libra, Aquarius and
first half of Sagittarius.

Quadruped signs are: Aries, Taurus, Leo, second half of
Sagittarius and first half of Capricorn.

Watery signs are : Cancer, Scorpio, Pisces and second
half of Capricorn.

Keeta Rasi or insect sign in Scorpio as per Garga and
Mantreswara. But’ Parasara includes Cancer also. Horasara
classifies the 3 watery signs as Keeta Rasi with particular
emphasis on Scorpio. Now, the first part of the sloka can
be well-conceived. Human signs are strong in the east or
ascendant. Biped signs are strong in south or the 10th.
Scorpio is strong in the West or the 7th while watery signs
(excluding Scorpio) have strength in the north or the 4th.
Similar view is found in Horasara of Prithuyasas (ch. I, s.12)
and Jataka Parijatha (ch. I, S. 16-18). The Kalabala of Rasis
are clear, as given in the text.

24. DAY AND NIGHT SIGNS—SIRSHODAYA AND
PRISHTODAYA SIGNS: Gemini, Cancer, Capricorn Aries,
Taurus and Sagittarius are nignt signs. Leo, Libra, Scorpio,
Aquarius, Pisces and Virgo are day signs. The signs Cancer,
Capricorn, Aries, Sagittarius and Taurus are called Prishtodaya
which rise with hind part. Sirodaya sigas (rising with head)
are: Leo, Libra, Scorpio, Virgo, Aquarius and Gemini. The
sign Pisces is Ubhayodaya (i.e. that rises with both head and
hind part).

25. STRENGTH OF RAST: If a Rasi is aspected by its
lord, or by a planet that is friendly to its lord or by Mercury or
by Jupiter, it is said to be strong. Planets other than the above
do not lend strength by aspect.

Lagna Thanu and Sakthi
Second Artha and Dhana
Third Sahaja and Parakrama
Fourth Bandhava and Griha
Fifth Putra and Pratibha
Sixth Ari and Vrana
Seventh Stri and Kama

Eighth Vinasa and Dehavivara
Ninth Punya and Guru
‘Tenth Karma and Mana (ara)
Eleventh Aya and Bhaya (714)
Twelfth Vyaya

Notes : The ascendant denotes the physique and vigour
of the native, The second house is indicative of money while
co-born and valour are to be noted from the 3rd. Residences
and relatives are governed by the 4th. The children and
intelligence are reflected by the Sth, Enemies and wounds
come under the 6th. Sexual acts and spouse fall under the
7th, The 8th house holds death. One’s past merits, preceptors
## Page 43

Chapter 3 39

and elders should be estimated from the 9th. Profession (work)
and honour are related to the 10th. Income and prosperity
are to be noted from the 11th while the last house highlights
expenses. For more detailed information, see pp 183-187 of
Horasara.

28-31 ADDITIONAL SYNONYMS.

The 4th (Vesma) and the 8th are called as Chaturasra
houses, The 9th is known as Tapa (az) i.e. penance. The 4th
hias names like Sukha (happiness), Jala (water), Patala (nether-
world). Bandhu (relatives) and Hibuka. The other names given
to the 10th house are : Karma (deed), Agna (command), Gagana
(sky or zenith) and Meshurana. The Sth and 9th are trines. The
Sth is the only house connected with Dhi (ie intellect) while the
9th house is Tritrikona, ic, the trine of trine. The 7thh ouse is
called Dyuna, Astha (setting), Jaayg(ara1) and Jamitra. The 6th
is Shatkona; the 3rd is Duschikya and the 12th Rippha, Kutumba
is the 2nd house.

Notes : The word Jamitram (afta) is derived from wat
and is indicative of the future goodluck of one’s wife. The
word is obviously connected with the Greek word diametron,

Regarding trines, only the Sth and the 9th are strictly
trines while the ascendant is not included in this classification.
## Page 44

40 Saravali

Our author uses the words “‘qafaatar” to indicate the first, Sth
and 9th houses separately in sloka 30 of this Chapter.
Such separate mention for the ascendant can be noticed
while the 5th and 9th are discussed, in Horasara and others.
Also refer to Jataka Parijata (Ch.1), Jataka Tatwa (1-27),
Lagna Chandrika (1-6), Brihat Jataka (Ch. 1), Phal Deepika
(1-17/18) and my English translations of Brihat Parsara Hora
(Ch. 8, sloka 35) and Horasara (Ch. 1, sloka 33). Thus, we
may know that the ascendant is not designated as a trine in any
standard astral literature.

32. KENDRA, APOKLIMA AND PANAPHARA-
EFFECTS-THEREOF : The adjoining houses with reference
to angles (Kendras) are Panaphara. The houses next to
Panapharas are Apoklima houses. The planets in angles give
effects in one’s boyhood. The effects of planets in Panapharas
are felt in the middle age while the planets in Apoklima give
result at the conclusion of the natives’s life,

Notes : Kendras are Ist, 4th, 7th and 10th houses. Pana-
pharas (also called cadent houses) are the 2nd, Sth, 8th and
11th, Apoklima houses (succedent) are the 3rd, 6th, 9th and
12th houses. The good or bad effects ate specially revealed in
the boyhood, youth and old age according to their placement
in angles, cadents or succedents.

35-36. EXALTATION AND FALL : Aries, Taurus, Capri-
corn, Virgo, Cancer, Pisces and Libra respectively are the signs
of exaltation for the Sun, Moon, Mars, Mercury, Jupiter, Venus
and Saturn. These are deeply exalted at 10, 3, 28, 15, 5, 27 and
20 degrees in the respective Rasis. The Rasis opposite exaltation
are the places of debilitation for the planets concerned, And the
respective degrees are of deep fall.

Notes : Planets derive strength by virtue of exaltation and
are weak if in fall. Even if a planet is in exaltation in Rasi but
in itsfallen Navamsa, its effects are neutralized. Conversely
though it may be in its debilitation Rasi, but in exaltation
Navamsa, its good effects only increase. Now, sce the table of
exaltation and fall for various planets :

Planet Deep exaltation Deep fall degree
degree
Sun Aries 10° Libra 10°
Moon Taurus 3° Scorpio 3°
Mars Capricorn 28° Cancer 28°
Mercury Virgo 15° Pisces i
Jupiter Cancer 5° Capricom 5°
Venus Pisces 27° Virgo 27°

Saturn Libra 20° Aries 20°

debilitation zones for Rahu and Ketu, Without bothering one-
self at this stage about the controversy, one can gather consoli-
dated information from my notes given on pages 20-21 of
Horasara.

37-38. LONG, MEDIUM AND SHORT ASCENSIONS
OF SIGNS : Pisces, Taurus, Aries and Aquarius are signs of
short ascension. Gemini, Sagittarius, Cancer, and Capricorn
are of medium ascension. The long ascension signs are :
Scorpio, Virgo, Leo and Libra. The head and other organs of
the native will be similar to the sign ascending at birth and
other relative signs. The planets occupying such houses will
also influence the form and shape of the various organs.

} Notes : If, for example, Scorpio ascends at birth, the head
of the native will be long. Should Aries rise, the head is small.
The influence lent by planets will also have a say on this
matter. For significations of organs, see next chapter.

In Jataka Parijatha, Ch. I, Pisces is stated to be of
medium ascension.

Also see Horasara, Ch. I, sloka 24,

40-41. COLOURS OF RASIS: From Aries onwards the
following 12 colours are allotted to the various Rasis respecti-
vely : red, white, green, pink, brown, grey, variegated, black,
golden, yellow, deep brown and white. If an idol of ‘the lord of
the ascendant is made in the colour alloted (as above) and is

worshipped, the native will destroy his enemies just as Lord
Indra destroyed the demons.

3-6. The counting of limbs according to the decanate
rising at birth should be identified as under :

If the first dezanate rises, count from head; if the second
decanate rises from neck and if the 3rd one rises, count from
pelvis. The 6 Rasis backwards from the ascendant denote the
left side of the body while the 6 forward Rasis from Lagna
indicate the right side of the body. Should the first decanate of
a sign ascend the lapsed part of the ascendant denotes left side
of the head and the part to rise yet indicates the right side of
the head, the 2nd and 12th denote right and left eyes respecti-
vely; the 3rd and 11th right and left ears; the 4th and 10th right
and left nose; the Sth and 9th right and left cheeks; the 6th and
8th right and left chins and the 7th left side of the face (by
area yet to rise) and the 7th right side of the face (by portion
already descended). If the 2nd decanate rises neck, shoulder,
arms, side, heart, stomach, and navel are to be understood in the
same order. Should the third decanate rise, pelvis, anus, penis,
## Page 49

Chapter 4 45

testicle, thigh, knee, calf, and feet will be counted in the same
order. The decanates occupied by malefics denote wounds etc.
while the ones by benefics indicate marks (or moles) on the
limbs concerned. Should these planets be in their own Rasi
or Amsa at birth, then the wound or mole are right from birth;
otherwise these will be caused later on (in appropriate
periods).

Notes : If the first decanate be rising, the limbs denoted
are as under :

Lagna — head —_(right/left side)
Qnd/12th =— eyes _—_(right/left)
3rd/11th _- ears (right/left)
4th/10th — nose —_(right/left side)
Sth/9th - cheeks (right/left)
6th/8th — chins —_(right/left)
1th — face — (right/left)

In the case of 2nd decanate ascending, the counting is
from neck, as under :

Lagna — neck —_(right/Left side)
2nd/12th — shoulder (right/left)
3rd/11th — arm —(rightyleft)
4th/10th — side —_(right/left)
sth/9th — heart —_(right/left side)
6th/8th — stomach (right/left side)
7th — navel (right/left side)

If the 3rd decanate ascends, then the arrangement takes
place from pelvis as under :

Lagnn— — _ pelvis (right/left)
2nd/12th = — —anus/penis (right/left)
3rd/llth  — testicle (cight/left)
4th/10th = — thigh (right/left)
sth/9th — knee (right/left)
6th/8th — calf (cight/left)

Tth = fer (right/left)

Ifa decanate is occupied by a malefic, say, Mars, there
will be wound etc. on the limb. A benefic denotes mole,
Should this be in a Rasi/Amsa owned by it, then the effect is
from birth itself. If not, this will occur in its dasa bhukti later
on.

7. PLANETARY PORTFOLIOS AND THEIR USE:
The Sun and the Moon are said to be the kings. Mercury
is the prince, Mars army chief, Jupiter and Venus ministers
while Saturn is servant. The native acquires such qualities as
of the strongest planet.

8. PLANETARY DIRECTIONS : The Sun, Venus,
Mars, Rahu, Saturn, the Moon, Mercury and Jupiter are
respectively the lords of the directions commencing from the
east.

Notes: The planetary rulerships of the 8 quarters are
clarified below :

1. The Sun-East 2. Saturn-West 3. Venus-South-east
4. The Moon-North-west 5. Mars-South 6. Mercury-North
7. Rahu-South-west 8. Jupiter-North-cast.

The directions are related to the zodiacal signs also vide
sloka 22, Ch. 3, supra.

9. PLANETARY NATURE : Jupiter, Mercury and Venus
are bencfics in nature. Saturn, Mars and the Sun are natural
malefics. Mercury in the company of malefics and the Moon
-f decreasing are also considered malefics,
## Page 51

Chapter 4 41

Notes: Thus, Jupiter and Venus are the only natural
benefics, Mercury, if not in the company of malefics, remains
a natural benefic. Otherwise, if he gets associated with natural
malefics, he turns into a malefic. As regards Moon, she is
benefic in the bright half and a malefic in dark half. Accord-
ing to some, she is good from bright half Dasami to Dark half
Panchami (See also sloka 16, Ch. 5, infra).

Apart from natural benefics and natural malefics, planets
are goodor bad according to the sign rising at birth, For
details, see my English translation of Brihat Parasara Hora,
(Ch. 34).

10-11. SYNONYMS OF PLANETS : Heli and Bhanu are
the other names given to the Sun. The Moon is called Sasi,
Krooradrik, Bhomisuta, Aara (rz), Rakta, and Vakra are
indicative of Mars. Hemna, Vid, Gna and Bodhana denote
Mercury. Eedya (£gq), ljya (gaz), Angira and Jiva all are
Jupiter’s names. Aasphujit, Sita (faa) and Bhrigu mean Venus.

Manda, Kona, Yama and Krishna are Saturn's synonyms.
For these planets, there are various other names which should
be elicited from other texts.

Notes: There are many other names with which the
planets are referred to in traditional astrological literature. The
curious reader may consult notes given under sloka 41, Ch. 2
of my English version of Horasara.

12-13, PLANETARY COLOURS, DEITIES AND
## Page 52

48 Saravali

THEIR USE : From the Sun onwards, the respective hues of
the planets are : copper-red, white, (blood) red, green, yellow,
variegated, and black. The deities for these planets are re
pectively: Fire, Water, Kartikeya, Vishnu, Indra, Sachi Devi
and Brahma. The planets from the Sun onwards should be
worshipped by the Mantras concerned and if trips to the
respective directions are undertaken, one can gain gold, gems,
elephants etc.

Notes : The colours described can be noted from Brihat
Parasara Hora Sastra (Ch. 1), Brihat Jataka (Ch, 11), Horasara

Phala Deepika (Ch. 11) etc.

The planetary directions are given in sloka 8, of this
chapter. If one undertakes a journey to the directions concerned
after worshipping a planet, he will stand to gain. For example,
one wants go to the northeast; he must worship the -planet
Jupiter (and also Indra) before proceeding. Then, he can
achieve his aim unhindered.

14, SEX, CASTE AND ELEMENTS :The Moon and
Venus are females. Mercury and Saturn rule neutrals (i.e.
these two are neutrals). Males are Jupiter, the Sun and
Mars. Brahmins are ruled by Jupiter and Venus. The Sun
and Mars preside over the royal lot. The Moon rules Vaisyas
(business community). Saturn rules those of mixed breed
while Mercury presides over Sudras, (the 4th caste people). The
five primordial compounds, viz. Fire, Barth, Ether, Water and
Air are respectively ruled by planets from Mars onwards.

18. USE OF THESE : In the matter of winning enemies,
delivery of child or such questions, materialization of the
objective concerned will be as per the period allotted to the
Lagna Lord. This should be understood according to the
ascendant passed,

Notes : Suppose Jupiter is the Lagna Lord ina query
relating to child birth, with the Prasna Lagna having passed
10 degrees. Jupiter indicates the period month as per the
previous sloka and hence one third of a month should pass
for the delivery to take place. Such information can be
elicited in regard to return of missing person etc. Rahu and
Ketu have not been allotted such periods by Kalyana Varma
in sloka 17, Ch. 4. Sarvartha Chintamani, however, denotes
8 months for Rahu and 3 months for Ketu, vide its chapter 3
sloka 90.

21, DESCRIPTION AND NATURE OF THE SUN: Thz
Sum has curly hair, sharp mind, prominent appearance, majestic
voice, and is not very tall. His eyes are honey-coloured. He is
courageous, steady, and of a complexion which has a mix of
red and green His feet are not conspicuous (i.e, small in size).
He is bilious and has sturdy bones. He is great and majestie,
He has fiery rays and square body, and wears safforn coloured
apparels.

Notes: The Sun has no hair on his head. He causes
reddish clouds. He denotes tuberculosis, fever, physique, head,
father, king etc. (Ref. Poorva Parasaryam).

Mantreswara also describes the Sua as dealt with in
various texts. He uses the words “qq a1g:’” which indicate
that the Sun has long hands. Kalyana Varma’s words qget
have been rendered as fiery rays asqq also denotes fire and
st the rays (or hands), Similarly, Prithuyasas has used
TEEKSHNAMSU in Horasara. The Sun has predominance of
Satwa. He is said not to live in one place for long. His
weakness causes damage to eyes,

If ina nativity, a satwik planet is strong, he will have
kindness, firmness, truthfulness, softness and respect for Gods
and the wise. If Rajasik planet is strong, he will be skilful
in poetry, literature, fine arts, sacrifices (religious), will have
interest in the fair sex and be valorous. If Tamasik planet is
strong, he will be short-tempered, foolish, indolent, and long-
sleeping. The Sun, the Moon and Jupiter are Satvic planets.
Mereury and Venus are Rajasic planets. Mars, Saturn and
‘Rahu are Tamasic planets. These descriptions are found in
our present work and in various other texts, in many contexts.
Now, the reader can easily understand these.

She has mellifluous voice. She is fair in complexion, has an

23. DESCRIPTION AND NATURE OF MARS : The
planet Mars is short; his eyes are reddish-brown in colour.
He has a strong body. He is as bright as burning fire. He is
not steady in disposition, He has marrow in bones and flesh.
He wears red-coloured apparels. He is more intelligent and
is courageous. He is an accomplished speaker (fatavarn).
He causes injury. He has short and shining hair. He is bilious
in disposition and is Tamasic. He is adventurous and wrath-
ful and is skilful in hurting. He is blood-red in appearance.

Notes: POORVA PARASARYAM states that Mars has

diseases caused by fire etc., kingdom, wheat, gold, coral, abdo-

Mars has slender waist. He has attractive limbs. (Ref.
Jataka Parijata, Ch. 1, sloka 55.)

He has rough voice and a depressed belly. He is modest.

25. DESCRIPTION AND NATURE OF JUPITER:
The eyes of Jupiter are somewhat reddish-brown. He is learned
in Vedas. His voice resembles that of a lion, He is a firm and
is prominently Satwic. His physical complexion is akin to pure
yellow metal. He has broad and prominent chest. He is always
fond of virtues and is modest. He has firm and large eyes
and is of forgiving disposition. He wears yellow apparels, is
phlegmatic, fat and pre-eminent.

Notes : “agtemeter” has been interpreted/by some comm-
entators as “wearing excellent rosaries”. This view cannot be
subscribed to, while I have rendered the same as having firm
and large eyes. See ag=firm, veHz——large and mer= eyes.

Jupiter has large eyes and hence his aspect on or occup-
tion of the 2nd house confers large and beautiful eyes.

He has large belly. He is a minister, has sharp mind,
and is gold-coloured. He denotes abdomen, wisdom, work,
hearing and auspiciousness. He consumes honey, ghee and
Sweet food. He is virtuous and meritorious and is an expon-
ent of mythology. He indicates happiness, Vedic rituals,
Sacrifices etc. He rules Brahmins, sages and ascetics and
possesses empirical disposition. (Vide Poorva Parasaryam).

27. DESCRIPTION AND NATURE OF SATURN :
Saturn has red and depressed eyes, emaciated body, prominent
veins, is indolent, black-bodied, and windy in temparament.
He is a tale-bearer, He is rhuscular, unkind, foolish, has large
nails and teeth, is very dirty, impure, Tamasic in disposition,
fierce, short-tempered and old (worn out). He adores black
apparels.

Now, we have to understand, the use. of these planetary
descriptions, qualities etc. as explained in the.foregoing slokas.
If a planet influences the ascendant, its lord, its ocoupant,
Moon sign lord, a bhava lord etc. the sphere, concerned
changes accordingly. For example, if the 7th lord is influenced
by Venus, the wife of the native acquires the qualities asoribed
to Venus. She may be beautiful, be of Rajasic. dispositio
intelligent, fortunate etc etc. If the ascendant or its lord comes
in contact with the Sun the native may be baldy, cousageous,
may like saffron apparels, may have sturdy bones, small feet,
and be susceptible to T.B., fever etc. Similar inferences may
be suitably made by the wise. :

28-29. NATURAL FRIENDSHIP, NEUTRALITY AND.
ENMITY BETWEEN PLANETS : The Sun’s friends are
Jupiter, Mars and the Moon, The Moon's friends are the Sun
and Mercury. The Sun, the Moon and Jupiter are friendly
to Mars. Venus and the Sun are Mercury’s friends. The
Sun, Moon and Mars are friendly disposed to Jupiter. Saturn
and Mercury are friends of Venus Mercury and Venus ‘are
Saturn's friends. The Sun’s enemies are Venus and Saturn.
The Moon has no enemies. Mercury is inimical to Mars
while the Moon is Mercury’s enemy. Venus and Mercury are
the enemies of Jupiter. The Moon andthe Sun are enemies
of Venus. Saturn's enemies are the Sun, the Moon and Mars.
If a planet is neither a friend nor an enemy of another one, there
exists neutrality among them.

30. TEMPORARY FRIENDSHIP AND ENMITY
BETWEEN PLANETS :1f a planet is in the 12th, 4th, 2nd,
## Page 61

Chapter 4 37

10th, 11th or 3rd from another planet, then there is temporary
friendship between the two. If the position is in the 6th, 7th,
8th, Ist, Sth, or the 9th, then there is temporary enmity among
them. (This may be applied to a birth horoscope, horary
horoscope or any such other context).

“31. FIVE KINDS OF CONSIDERATIONS OF RELA-
TIONSHIP : (a) Should there be temporary friensdhip and
natural friendship between two planets, then they become
extremely friendly (afafiq7). (b) If there is natural neutrality
and temporary friendship, there exists only friendship between
two planets, (c) If there is natural enmity and temporary
friendship, they are neutral in relationship. (d) Should they
be naturally neutral and temporarily inimical, they are only
inimical. (¢) If there is enmity both naturally and tempora-
rily, then they are greatly inimical to each other.

Notes: These rules are simple and need no clarification.
However, an example is given thus: Suppose the Sun is in
Taurus and Jupiter is in Cancer. They are mutually in 3rd
and 11th, Hence, they are temporary friends in the nativity.
They are by nature friendly to each other. Hence on account
of these two sources of friendship, they become mutually
extreme friends as far as the concerned horoscope is concerned.
Now, see point (e) above. The Sun and Saturn are mutually
inimical. If these two are mutually in 6/8 positions in a chart,
they act in a highly inimical manner for each other.

32-33. PLANETARY ASPECTS : Planets lend 1/4th
aspect on the 3rd and 10th, half aspect on the 4th and 8th,
3/4 th aspect on Sth and 9th and full aspect on the 7th, from
their positions. Saturn has special full aspect on the 3rd
and 10th, Jupiter on the Sth and the 9th and Mars on the 4th
and 8th. All planets aspect the 7th fully.

34, PLANETARY STRENGTHS : To assess the auspici-
ous and inauspicious effects of a planet, its directional, posi-
tional, temporal and motional strengths are important; for,
without these, it is considered to be weak.

35, DIRECTIONAL AND POSITIONAL STRENGTHS :
Jupiter and Mercury have directional strength while in the
ascendant (i.e. East), the Sun and Mars in the 10th (i.e. South),
Saturn in the 7th (i.e, West) and the Moon and Venus in the
4th (ie, North). If a planet is in exaltation, Mulatrikona,
own house, friendly house or own Navamsa and aspected by
a benefic, it assumes strength. The Moon and Venus are
strong in even Rasis while the rest are so in odd Rasis. This
is called positional strength.

Notes: Digbala or directional strength is found thus :
Take the case of Jupiter. He gets full strength, under this
heading, of 60 shashtiamsas, if he is on the cusp of the ascend-
ant. If he is on the seventh cusp (ie. 7th Bhava Madhya), his
Digbala is nil, In other places, it should be worked out by
rule of three process.

To speak deeply, Sthana Bala or positional strength is
made up of:
## Page 63

Chapter 4 38

(a) Uchcha Bala (cxaltation strength)

(b) Sapta Vargaja Bala

(c) Ojayugma Rasyamsa Bala (i.e. strength on account of
odd and even Rasis and such Navamsas)

(4) Kendra Bala (angles)

(ec) Drekkana Bala (Decanates)

These five kinds of strength denote the positional strength
ofa planet, which from part of shadbala, For fuller information,
please see Ch. 27 and Ch. 28 of my English version of BRIHAT
PARASARA HORA SASTRA.

36. TEMPORAL AND MOTIONAL STRENGTHS:
The Sun, Jupiter and Venus acquire strength during day time
while Saturn, the Moon and Mars become strong during night
time, Mercury acquires vigour at all times. The Horabala goes
to Hora lord. masa bala (ntq¢—=month) to the lord of the month,
Dina bala to the lord of the week day of birth and Abda (year)
bala is credited to the lord of the year of birth. Malefies get
strength in Dark Half while benefics become strong in Bright
Half. The planet that is victorious in war, that is in its retro-
gtade motion, or that is not combust become strong. The lumi-
naries get strength in northern course. This is how Satyacharya
detailed motional strength.

Notes : Each day from one Sun rise to the next one is
divided into 24 horas (or hours), The planet ruling the hour
of birth is called Hora'lord and gets 60 shashtiamsas. The. first
hora of the day is ruled by the lord of the week day itself.. For
example, Mars rules the opening hora of Tuesday. The second
one is ruled by the lord of the sixth week day. The third one is
tuled by lord of the sixth week day counted from the second
hora lord. Still an easy method is suggested here, so that the
## Page 64

60 Saravali

reader need not memorise or make cumbersome calculations.
Just note the first hora lord and count every alternative week
day lord backwards. You get the hora lord successively. For
example, Saturday has first hora ruled by Saturn, second by
Jupiter, third by Mars, fourth by the Sun and so on and so
forth. And calculations of Kala Hora should be done with
reference to Mean local time.

TaRAaA Tear: PREAH TAAL aA: |
ard afarefagat gastt afar: caaiea: wae

37. AYANA BALA : Venus, Mars, the Sun and Jupiter
are strong in Uttarayana while the Moon and Saturn are strong
in Dakshinayana. Mercury is strong in both the cases. This is
called Ayana Bala.

38. DREKKANA BALA: Male planets are strong in the
first decanate, female planets in the third decanate and neutral

planets in the second decanate ofa Rasi. Planets are strong
only when they are away from the Sun, as per Yavanas

39. TRIBHAGA BALA OR TRIAMSA BALA : The
Moon, Venus and Mars get this strength in the first, second
and third parts of the night respectively. This is similarly
enjoyed by Mercury, the Sun and Saturn in day time while
Jupiter has it always irrespective of day or night.

Notes : (a) Whether it is day birth or night birth, Jupiter
gets 60 shashtiamsas of Triamsa Bala, (b) Additionally, one of
Moon, Venus and Mars, or one of Mercury, Sun and Saturn
get this strength according to birth being in night or day.

For Example, there occurs a birth at 14 ghatis after night
fall while the night duration is 30 ghatis. $o to say, birth is in
the second one third of the night. As suggested, the strength
## Page 65

Chapter 4 61
of 60 shashtiamsas, on this score goes to Venus, This is again
60 shashtiamsas.

warnfamartagarara fart STH: weott

40. NAISARGIKA BALA (NATURAL STRENGTH) :
Saturn, Mars, Mercury, Jupiter, Venus, Moon and Sun are
stronger than the other in the ascending order. (This is called
natural strength). Should there be similarity in other strengths,
then the one with greater natural strength prevails,

Notes : Naisargika bala accrues to a planet according to
its brightness, This is constantly expressed and is not variable,
The Sun is the most luminous body and hence its natural
strength is the highest. The darkest body Saturn gets the least.
See the following table for an easy grasp :

Sun : 1.000 Rupa
Moon 0.857 Rupa
Mars a 0.286 Rupa
Mercury: 0.429 Rupa
Jupiter: 0.571 Rupa
Venus : 0.714 Rupa
Saturn 5 0.143 Rupa

(One Rupa equals 60 Shashtiamsas)

2-4, AVASTHAS OR STATES OF PLANETS: Planets
have nine states of being, viz. Deepta, Svastha, Mudita, Santa,
Sakta, Nipeedita, Bhita, Vikala and Khala, A planet in its exal-
tation is said to be in Deeptavastha, In its own house, it is in
Svasthavastha, friendly house -Muditavastha, in beneficial
Vargas Santavastha, with bright rays Saktavastka, in combus-
tion Vikalavastha, if defeated in planetary war Nipeedita, in
malefic Vargas Khalavastha, and if in fall in Bhitavastha.

Notes : The indications of the above mentioned Avasthas
are given below :

Deepta (at) = radiant
Svastha —(#aza) = confident
Mudita (afea) = rejoiced
Santa (ava) = peaceful

Sakta (aaa) = strong
## Page 67

Chapter 4 63

Nipeedita (fatifsa) = oppressed or hurt
Bhita (ata) = alarmed
Vikala (fasq) = mutilated

With the help of the said explanations, we can easily
understand the effects such planets will reveal.

The Sun and the Moon are not subjected to Nipeedita
state as they do not involve in planetary war. Vikalavastha
does not apply to the Sun for he does not get combust but is
the cause of combustion. Saktavastha can however be applied
to the Sun too as he is obscured in solar eclipse.

Apart from the said nine states, Sanketa Nidhi enlists 12
kinds of different states of planets. Please see for more details,
Ch. V ibid.

There are 27 Graha Samayas (wgqaa) i.e. planetary

conditions. These will help us know asto what a planet is
doing at a particular moment, with reference to cither birth or
query. Such positions reveal specifie results. How to calculate
these positions and the effects thereof are noted below :

Find out the number of signs from Aries to ascendant.
Again find out in what number of sign, the planet for which
waa (Samaya) is required, counted from Aries. Multiply these
figures mutually and again the latest product be multiplied by
the total number of Dasa period years of the planet as per
Vimshottari dasa scheme. Divide this by 27 and the remainder
indicates Graha Samaya (Some scholars, however, advise that
the planet’s position is to be counted trom Lagna instead of
Aries. It is wrong counting the planet’s position from

. Aries as the sloka clearly says 3arfefeaatatiq vide Jotisharnava
Nayaneetam) Let us assume that in Virgo Lagna chart,
the Moon is in Sagittarius. Hence, we count six signs
from Aries through Virgo Ascendant and get 6. Again from
Aries to Sagtttarius (Moon sign) we get 9. Multiply 9 by 6 to
get 54. The dasa period of the Moon is 10 as per Vimshottari
dasa. When we multiply 54 by 10, we get 540. This when
## Page 68

64 Saravali
divided by 27 yields no balance and hence the 27th Samaya is
denoted.

Now the scheme of Samayas and their effects :

1. Sana: good family, children, respect, success and
position,

2. Vastradharana: precious stones, money, position and
clothes.

3. Pundradharana : dear to people, gains in foreign count-
ries, hard work and honour.

4. Upadesa: lands, conveyances and happiness.

5. Siva Pooja : fond of lands, royal wrath, expenses and
litigations.

6. Aaposana : wealth, fond of wicked people.

7. Vishnvarchana : bile, grief, highly learned.

8. Vipraradhana : fortune, gains from lands, success over
enemies, rich relatives.

9, Namaskara : soft-spoken, Conveyances and Capability
to speak on cither side in arguments,

10. Adri Pradakshina : bilious diseases, dysentery,
tions and penalties.

11, Vaisyadeva : position with king, good family, peren-
nial progress.

itiga-

12, Athidhi Satkara: Cheat, jimmicks and monetary
gains.

13. Bhojana : sick, dismissed from the circle, cheating.

14, Ambhapana : bad meal, bad'acts.

15. Ahamkara : egoism and enmity with people.

16. Tamboola : good position, high learning, money and
fame of high order.

17, Nripalapa : respect, pions disposition, diviee cows.

18. Kireetadharana: big position in army, learned,
wealthy.
## Page 69

Chapter 5 65
19. Ekanta Sambhashana : lazy, soft-spoken.
20. Aalasya : abundant education, lazy, careless.

21. Sayana : very .short-tempered, sick, disputes in
family.

22. Amritapana : foolish, harmful, blaming elders, des-
truction (Some texts prescribe good results which only seem to
be sensible.)

23. Madhupana: health, good children, beautiful wife,
rich food.

24, Dhanarjana : respect, much wealth, skilful.

25. Bhikshatana : loss, bad teaching.

26. Nidra : long lasting diseases, drunkard.

27. Sambhoga: attached to base women, cunning and
revengeful.

aha facie gaa: sarafaearfiaaafcgat: 1
werarfafgatal ararrae RT ATES: UU

5. EFFECTS OF A RADIANT PLANET: Should a
planet be in Deepta state (radiant) at birth the native burns his
enemies with the fire of his valour. He gathers all kinds of
wealth. His (band of) elephants soak the surface of the earth
with the juice or ichor exuding from their temples. (That is, the
native will own a large number of elephants. See the simulta-
neous literary ability of Kalyana Varma. A number of such
comparisons can be found in this work.)

Note : Please see notes under sloka 13 of this chapter for
more information.

14. RETROGRESSION IN EXALTATION: If a
planet is retrograde while in exaltation, it produces no effects
(ie. nothing good will happen). This is the view held by some.
Even if it is in exaltation by its entry in retrograde motion
from the next sign, (for example, Jupiter entering Cancer from
Leo), the effect is same, for it takes unduly long time in such
traversion.

Notes : afaam indicates a planet (i.e. from Mars to
Saturn) entering the previous sign while in its (R) motion, for
example from Taurus to Aries.

Many writers hold the view that a planet if be retrograde
while in exaltation loses its potence and conversely if in fall
while in its retrograde motion, it acquires strength and acts
favourably.

15. DIFFERENT EFFECTS: A planet in exaltation is
considered highly strong. It is medium in strength in its
Mulatrikona Rasi or own house. Its strength is only nominal
if it be aspected by a friendly planet or be in a friendly Rasi.

Notes : The idea behind the suggestion is that a planet in
a friendly Rasi or with a friendly planet’s aspect is not superior
to the one in its Moolatrikona Rasi while the one occupying
its Moolatrikona Rasi is second in strength to the planet that
is in its exaltation.

16-17. The elders among Yavanas say that the Moon is
of medium strength for ten days commencing from Sukla
Padyami, i.e. first day of Bright Lunar Half. During the
following ten days (ie. from the llth day or Ekadasi of
Bright Lunar Half through the Sth day or Panchami of Dark
Lunar Half or Krishna Paksha), she is exceedingly strong.
And during the third ten-day period (ic. from the 6th day or
Shashti of Dark Lunar Half through the New Moon day or
Amavasya) she has very little strength. If at birth the Moon
has brilliant rays, is bright circled and full, it makes the native
an unencounterable king.

Notes: saet—=bright. vsq—= circle or disc of the
Sun/Moon, and hence it is “‘bright-circled””.

This sloka highlights the importance of full Moon in a
horoscope.

18. GOOD RESULTS IN MID-LIFE: If at birth the

lord of Moon sign or the lord of the ascendant or Jupiter be in
Kendra (angle), the native is happy in the middle of his life.

Notes: Prithuyasas in Horasara states that if the lord of
the Mooi sign or the lord of the ascendant be in angle along
with Jupiter, the native becomes happy in the middle of his
life (See Ch. 16, sloka 14). Kalyana Varma stipulates that
Jupiter in angle singly is enough to cause the said. results.

19-20. The effects revealed by various Rasis will corres-
pond to the strengths of their lords. Should two planets have
identical strength, the one with higher Naisarga bala (natural
strength-vide sloka 40, Ch. IV supra) will prevail. According
to Chudamani Acharya the ascendant's strength equals that
of its lord.

Notes : Suppose, the lagaa lord and 6th lord have equal
strength in a Leo Lagna chart, the lord of Lagna being the Sun
and the 6th lord being Saturn. Among theso two, the Sun has
more Naisarga bala than Saturn and hence the native is stron-
ger than his enemies.

21-24, SWAKSHETRA, MULATRIKONA ETC. : In
Leo, upto 20 degrees, it is the Sun’s Mulatrikona and the rest
is his own house. The Moon’s exaltation zone is the first 3°
of Taurus, with the remaining portion being her Mulatrikona.
Upto 12° in Aries, Mars is in Mulatrikona. The rest is his
own house. Mercury in Virgo has the first 15° as exaltation,
the next 5° (ie. 15° 1’ to 20°) as Mulatrikona and the remai
ing portion is termed is own house. In Sagittarius, first 10°
is Jupiter's Mulatrikona, with the rest being own house. The
first 5° in Libra ig Mulatrikona of Venus and the balance his
## Page 76

n : Saravalt
own house. Aquarius is Mulatrikona for Saturn im the

initial 20 degree portion (as the Sun has in Leo) and the last
10° in Aquarius is his own house.

Notes: Mercury is the only one planet that is exalted
in its own house, Hence, in Virgo, it has first 15 degrees as
its exaltation, the next 5 degrees as Mulatrikona zone is a
stronger placement in preference to its own house zone, ‘The
exaltation zone is still superior.

25. EFFECTS OF EXALTED PLANETS ETC.: If a
planet is exalted, it gives auspicious results, to full extent. It
is futile if in debilitation. The results are limited in an enemy's
camp. The auspicious effects given by a planet are 1/4th ina
friendly house, + in own house and 3/4th in Mulatrikona Rasi.

Notes: The effects revealed by a planet are: 25% of its
full capacity if in a friendly house, 50% in own house, 75% in
Mulatrikona and 100% in exaltation house. In enemy’s camp,
it is less than 25%. Thus its status gradually increases as under :
Enemy's house, friendly camp, own house or Swakshetra,
Mulatrikona and exaltation Rasi. These positions become
better in the ascending order. While in debilitation, it gives
no auspicious effects.

Neecha Bhanga Raja Yoga, is however a different aspect,
and should not be handy for all practical purposes.

26. INAUSPICIOUSNESS OF PLANETS: A planet is
fully inauspicious if it is in its debilitation; it is somewhat
house (than in debilitation). Its inauspicious
it is exalted, 3/4th in friendly house, 4 in own
house and 4th in Mulatrikona Rasi,

Notes: This isa converse process while the previous
sloka explains auspicious results. The inauspicious effects are
100% in debilitation, somewhat less if in inimical Rasi, nil if
exalted, 75% in friendly Rasi, 50% in own house and 25% in
Mulatrikona, Draw a comparison as under :

Position Good Bad
Debilitation Nil 100%
Inimical limited better than fall
Friendly 25% 15%,
Swakshetra 50% 50%
Mulatrikona 715% 25%
Exaltation 100% nil

For example, from the two slokas in question, we can
infer that if a Swakshetra planet can be auspicious to the extent
of 50%, a planet in friendly house can give good effects only
to the tune of 25%.

28-30. EFFECTS ACCORDING TO EXALTATION
ETC. : A planet in exaltation gives all kinds of wealth. It
confers ministership or leadership over army, if in Mulatrikona
Rasi, If it is in own house, it gives happiness, money, grains,
wealth etc. In a friendly house, it gives fame, splendour,
abundant good fortune (mfaaai), long-lasting wealth and also
wealth through king. A planet that is in its own hora makes
one courageous.

Notes: The word “Hora” in sloka 30 is generally
interpreted as house so that it applies to all the seven planets.
But, in this context, in sloka 29, ‘‘own house” has already
been discussed and hence, the word “‘Hora” in sloka 30 means
“half” i.e. lunar or solar hora. Thus, the last line of sloka 30
should be applied only to the position of the Sun and that of
the Moon. This is the strict translation aspect, while in
practical aspect, ‘‘hora” can mean house and a person can be
valorous if a planet is in own house (or if the luminaries are
in their own hora).

31-33. A planet in its own decanate confers virtues
while the one in own Navamsa makes one famous. Courage,
wealth and fame are bestowed by a planet occupying its own
Sapthamsa. One becomes devout and helpul if a planet is in its
own Dvadasamsa, A planet in own Trimsamsa gives happiness
and good qualities. When a planet is aspected by a benefic
planet, the native becomes wealthy, famous, fortunate, chief
of all, beautiful and happy.

divisions in the earlier chaptcrs. Different uses are to be suita-

34-35, If a planet is with ojha or Yugma Bala (i.e. strength
by being in male or female Rasis), the native is worshipped by
the public, expert in arts, pleased, immune to sickness and
prone to fear of other worlds. A planet with positional
strength gives perennial happiness, friendship, courage, fixity
of mind and independent profession or work.

Notes: The Moon and Venus get cach half rupa by
staying in an even Rasi. Another half rupa is obtained by
their stay in even Navamsa. Should they be in odd Rasi or
Navamsa, their score is nil on this count. Similarly, odd
Rasis and odd Navamsas give half rupa each, for the rest of the
S planets. This strength is designated as ojhayugma Rasyamsa
bala (or strength by oddjeven Rasi and Navamsa position) as
shown under the heading positional strength, vide notes for
sloka 35, Ch, IV.

36-38. A planet with directional strength takes the
native to the direction ruled by it and gives clothes, jewels,
conveyances etc. And the native is happy in such a direction.
A planet with Ayana Bala similarly takes t'e native to its
direction and confers various kinds of wealth apart from fame.
In both the cases, the planets should not be combust or
debilitated. If a planet has Cheshta Bala, it sometimes gives
kingdom, sometimes respect; sometimes money and yet some-
times increases the fame of the native.

Notes: We have already explained Digbala or direc-
tional strength, vide notes under sloka 35 of Chapter 4. Suppose,
Saturn is in the 7th, without combustion or debilitation, then
it takes one towards west (see sloka 8, Ch.4) and gives success.
Similarly, Ayana Bala and Cheshta Bala are explained in
slokas 36-37 of the previous chapter.

39, EFFECTS OF RETROGRADE PLANETS : A benefic
if retrograde is strong and is capable of conferring kingdom.
If a malefic is retrograde, it causes grief and purposeless
wandering.

Note : According to Bhavartha Ratnakara, a malefic does
good if in retrogression, see sloka 16, Ch. 13. But Jataka Tatwa
(A-71) attributes strength equal to exaltation to all such
planets irrespective of being malefic or benefic.

41. DIVA BALA AND RATRI BALA : A planet that
has Diva bala or Ratri bala is eapable of conferring lands,
elephants etc, Such a native defeats his enemies with courage
and achieves kingdom and wealth.

Notes: Diva Ratri bala is also called Nathonnatha Bala
which forms part of Kala Bala. Mars, Saturn and the Moon
get this at night while Jupiter, Venus and the Sun get this
during day. Mercury is strong inday and in night. For
details, see my English version of BRIHAT PARASARA
HORA SASTRA.
